## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology
**Analysis**: This task belongs to population ecology and mathematical biology, focusing on deterministic demographic models. The growth rate dP_dt is typically governed by density-dependent feedback mechanisms acting on the current population P and may be modulated by time t through environmental or seasonal forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unrestricted exponential growth)
- Logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (self-limiting growth toward carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P)) (growth decelerates logarithmically with population size)
- Theta-logistic model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible inflection point near carrying capacity)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (population declines below a critical threshold)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) * (1 - c2 * P) (enhanced per-capita growth at low density)
- Linear relaxation: dP_dt = c0 * (c1 - P) (proportional convergence to equilibrium size)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (periodic environmental fluctuations)
- Exponential environmental forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (time-dependent resource availability)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 (density regulation with constant extraction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent regulation → Polynomial terms in P (linear + quadratic or higher-order negative feedback)
- Carrying capacity convergence → Product structure P * f(c*P) where f decreases toward zero
- Allee effect threshold → Cubic polynomial in P exhibiting sign reversal at low population sizes
- Seasonal environmental cycles → Trigonometric modulation (sin/cos) of intrinsic growth parameters
- Asymmetric growth inflection → Logarithmic or power-law transformations of P in the density term
- External harvesting/exploitation → Additive constant or proportional subtraction from baseline growth
- Time-varying resource availability → Multiplicative or additive functions of t scaling the growth rate
- Per-capita rate scaling → Implied P*f(P) structure where f represents density-dependent per-capita growth

**Ground Truth Analysis:**
GT symbolic expression: `c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*(c9 - exp(-c10*P))*P`
Let's expand and simplify the GT expression.
Variables: `P` (and `t` is mentioned in feature variables but not in the expression, so it's static w.r.t `t`).
Constants: `c0` to `c10`.
Let's group terms by powers of `P` and the exponential term.
Term 1: `c0 * (-c1 + P/c2) * (c3 - P/c4) * P`
= `c0 * (-c1*c3 + c1*P/c4 + c3*P/c2 - P^2/(c2*c4)) * P`
= `c0 * (-c1*c3*P + (c1/c4 + c3/c2)*P^2 - 1/(c2*c4)*P^3)`
= `-c0*c1*c3*P + c0*(c1/c4 + c3/c2)*P^2 - c0/(c2*c4)*P^3`

Term 2: `c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P`
= `c5*c6*P - c5/c7*P^2`

Term 3: `c8*(c9 - exp(-c10*P))*P`
= `c8*c9*P - c8*P*exp(-c10*P)`

Combining all terms:
GT = `(-c0/(c2*c4)) * P^3 + (c0*(c1/c4 + c3/c2) - c5/c7) * P^2 + (-c0*c1*c3 + c5*c6 + c8*c9) * P - c8 * P * exp(-c10*P)`

So the GT is a cubic polynomial in `P` plus a term of the form `k * P * exp(-a * P)`.
Specifically: `A * P^3 + B * P^2 + C * P + D * P * exp(-E * P)`
where `A, B, C, D, E` are constants derived from `c0...c10`.
Note that `D = -c8` and `E = c10`.
The structure is exactly: `P * (A * P^2 + B * P + C + D * exp(-E * P))`
Or `P^3 * A + P^2 * B + P * C + P * D * exp(-E * P)`.

Let's check the candidates. They are mostly polynomials, exponentials, logs, etc.
We need to find a candidate that can represent `P^3 * c_a + P^2 * c_b + P * c_c + P * c_d * exp(c_e * P)`.

or equivalent forms that simplify to this.

Let's verify Candidate 3 again carefully.
Expression: `P*(P**2*c0 + P*c1 + c2*(c3*exp(P*c4) + 1) + c5)`
Expand:
`P * P**2 * c0` = `c0 * P**3`
`P * P * c1` = `c1 * P**2`
`P * c2 * c3 * exp(P*c4)` = `c2*c3 * P * exp(P*c4)`
`P * c2 * 1` = `c2 * P`
`P * c5` = `c5 * P`
Sum: `c0*P**3 + c1*P**2 + (c2+c5)*P + c2*c3*P*exp(P*c4)`
This is exactly `A*P**3 + B*P**2 + C*P + D*P*exp(E*P)`.
GT is `A'*P**3 + B'*P**2 + C'*P + D'*P*exp(-E'*P)`.
Mapping:
`c0 = A'`
`c1 = B'`
`c2 + c5 = C'`
`c2 * c3 = D'`
`c4 = -E'`
All constants are free, so we can always find values for `c0, c1, c2, c3, c4, c5` to match any `A', B', C', D', E'`.
Thus, Candidate 3 is a MATCH.

Let's double check GT structure one more time.
GT: `c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*(c9 - exp(-c10*P))*P`
= `P * [ c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4) + c5*(c6 - P/c7) + c8*(c9 - exp(-c10*P)) ]`
Inside brackets:
`c0*(-c1*c3 + c1*P/c4 + c3*P/c2 - P^2/(c2*c4))` -> quadratic in P
`+ c5*c6 - c5*P/c7` -> linear in P
`+ c8*c9 - c8*exp(-c10*P)` -> constant + exponential
So inside brackets is: `A*P^2 + B*P + C + D*exp(-E*P)`
Multiply by P: `A*P^3 + B*P^2 + C*P + D*P*exp(-E*P)`
Matches Candidate 3 exactly.

One minor point: Candidate 3 has `c2*(c3*exp(P*c4) + 1)`. This gives `c2*c3*exp(...) + c2`.
When multiplied by P, it gives `c2*c3*P*exp(...) + c2*P`.
This fits `D*P*exp(...) + C*P` where `C` gets a contribution from `c2`. The remaining `P` coefficient comes from `c5`. So `C = c2 + c5`. This is perfectly flexible.

Thus, Candidate 3 is definitely a match.

### Ground Truth Analysis
The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*(c9 - exp(-c10*P))*P`

GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*(c9 - exp(-c10*P))*P
Candidates evaluated: 54

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

## GT Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
0.17*(P/1.047 - 1)*(1 - P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 - P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 - exp(-0.097*P))*P
```

Let me expand this. Let me use approximate values: a = 0.17, b = 1.047, d = 10.21, k = 0.097.

**Term 1:** `a*(P/b - 1)*(1 - P/d)*P`
= a*(P/b - 1)*(1 - P/d)*P

**Term 2:** `a*(1 - P/d)*P`

**Term 3:** `a*(1 - exp(-k*P))*P`

Combine Terms 1 and 2:
= a*(1 - P/d)*P * [(P/b - 1) + 1]
= a*(1 - P/d)*P * (P/b)
= a*P²/b * (1 - P/d)
= a*P²/b - a*P³/(b*d)

So the polynomial part is: `a*P²/b - a*P³/(b*d)`

Term 3: `a*P - a*P*exp(-k*P)`

Total GT = -a/(b*d) * P³ + a/b * P² + a*P - a*P*exp(-k*P)

With numerical values:
- Coefficient of P³: -0.17/(1.047*10.21) ≈ -0.01590
- Coefficient of P²: 0.17/1.047 ≈ 0.16237
- Coefficient of P: 0.17
- Exponential term: -0.17*P*exp(-0.097*P)

So GT = c_3*P³ + c_2*P² + c_1*P - a*P*exp(-k*P)

The key basis functions are: **P³, P², P, P*exp(-kP)** where k > 0 (so for P ≥ 0, exp(-kP) is a decaying exponential).

Now I need to check which candidates can match this structure. The critical feature is the **P*exp(-kP)** term (with negative exponent coefficient).

Let me categorize the candidates by their basis functions:

For a match, I need candidates that contain:
1. A cubic polynomial in P (P³, P², P terms)
2. A term like P*exp(cP) where c can be negative
3. Possibly a constant term (which should be 0 in GT since GT(0)=0)

Let me check GT(0): all terms have P as factor, so GT(0) = 0. Any candidate with a free constant can set it to 0.

Now let me check each candidate systematically.

**Key distinction:** The GT has `P*exp(-kP)` as a basis function. Many candidates use `exp(cP)` (without the P multiplier), `log(cP+1)`, `sin(...)`, `cos(...)`, or `|P|` terms. These are fundamentally different basis functions and cannot match.

Let me identify candidates with the right structure:

This has P³, P², P, and P*exp(c4*P). Setting c4 < 0 gives the decaying exponential. This matches the GT structure! Let me verify:
- P³ coefficient: c0
- P² coefficient: c1
- P coefficient: c2 + c5
